### 1.
Has \(A^2\), \(A\), \(\exp(A\cdot)\), and \(\log(\cdots)\). You can zero out exp/log terms, but then you only have \(A^2\) and \(A\) (and constant via log if not zeroed), cannot create \(A^{1/3}\) or \(\sqrt A\). **No.**

### 2.
\(\;c0\,A^{1/3}+c1\,A^2+c2\,A+c3\exp(Ac4)\).
Can set \(c3=0\) to remove exp and \(c2=0\) to remove \(A\). Then you get only \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^2\), but GT also needs \(-0.2013\sqrt A\). No way to generate \(\sqrt A\). **No.**

### 3.
Rational functions with denominators \(A^4(\cdot)+A^3(\cdot)+A(\cdot)+1\). To match a polynomial/monomial sum for all \(A\), denominators must be constant 1; but the shared parameter \(c2\) appears in multiple denominator terms and cannot generally eliminate all \(A\)-dependence while keeping needed numerators. Even if you force denominator to 1, the remaining terms are powers \(A^6,A^3,A,1\), not \(A^{1/3},A^{1/2},A^2\). **No.**

All terms divided by \(\sqrt(A)c1+1\) plus some \(\exp(Ac4)\) terms. To remove the denominator dependence you’d need \(c1=0\), making denominator 1. Then you have powers \(A^{5/2},A^{3/2},\sqrt A, A^2, A, 1\) and possibly exponentials. You can zero many coefficients, but you cannot create \(A^{1/3}\). **No.**

- No constant term, no exponential, no sin/cos, no log
- No dependence on t
- The basis functions are A^(1/3), A^(1/2), A^2

Let me go through candidates:

**Candidate 1:** A²c0 + Ac1 + c2*exp(Ac3) + c4*log(c5*exp(c6*sin(Ac7+c8))+1)
Has A² and A terms. Setting c1=0 removes A. But we need A^(1/3) and A^(1/2), which aren't available. The log-exp-sin term cannot produce power functions. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 2:** A^(1/3)*c0 + A²*c1 + A*c2 + c3*exp(A*c4)
Has A^(1/3) and A². Set c2=0 (remove A), c3=0 (remove exp). Left with A^(1/3)*c0 + A²*c1. Missing sqrt(A). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 3:** Rational function of polynomials in A. This is a rational function - ratio of polynomials. The GT has irrational powers (A^(1/3), A^(1/2)), which rational functions of A cannot produce. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 4:** Has A^(5/2), A^(3/2), sqrt(A), A², A, constants, exp terms, all divided by (sqrt(A)*c1+1). Let me simplify. Setting c4=0 removes exp terms. Then we have:
(A^(5/2)*c0 + A^(3/2)*c2 + sqrt(A)*c3*0 + A²*c5 + A*c6 + c7) / (sqrt(A)*c1 + 1)

Wait, with c4=0, exp(0)=1, so the exp terms become constants absorbed into other terms. Let me reconsider.

Actually with c4=0: exp(A*0)=1, so sqrt(A)*c3*1/(sqrt(A)*c1+1) and c8*1/(sqrt(A)*c1+1).

So we get: (A^(5/2)*c0 + A^(3/2)*c2 + sqrt(A)*c3 + A²*c5 + A*c6 + c7 + c8) / (sqrt(A)*c1 + 1)

This is a polynomial in sqrt(A) divided by (c1*sqrt(A)+1). This produces rational functions of sqrt(A), not A^(1/3). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 5:** c0 + c1*|A|^c2 + c3*(c4+|A|^c5)^c6 * |A|^c5
With A≥0, |A|=A. So: c0 + c1*A^c2 + c3*(c4+A^c5)^c6 * A^c5

Can we match GT? We need A^(1/3), A^(1/2), A^2.
Set c0=0, c2=1/2 → c1*A^(1/2). 
Remaining: c3*(c4+A^c5)^c6 * A^c5 needs to give A^(1/3) - 0.201*A^2.
This is a single term - it can't produce two independent power-law terms unless the (c4+A^c5)^c6 expansion works. But this is a single nonlinear expression, not a sum of two terms. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 6:** Rational in A with exp terms. Has A³, A², A, exp, constants over (Ac1+c2). Setting c7=0 removes exp. Then polynomial/linear in A. Can't produce A^(1/3) or A^(1/2). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 7:** c0 + c1*|A|^c2 + c3*exp(c4*sin(Ac5+c6))
With A≥0: c0 + c1*A^c2 + c3*exp(c4*sin(Ac5+c6)). The exp(sin) term is periodic/oscillatory, can't match power functions over all A. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 8:** Has t dependence: c4*t/(Ac5+c6). Setting c4=0 removes t. Left with A²c0+Ac1+c2*exp(Ac3)+c7/(Ac5+c6). No A^(1/3) or A^(1/2). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 9:** A²c0+Ac1+c2*exp(Ac3)+c4*exp(Ac5)*cos(Ac6). Exponential and trig, no fractional powers. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 10:** Ac0 + Ac1/(Ac2+c3) + c4*sin(Ac5+c6) + c7/(Ac2+c3). Rational in A plus sin. No fractional powers. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 11:** c0+c1*sin(Ac2+c3)+c4*log(c5*exp(c6*sin(Ac7+c8))+1). Trig/log, no power functions. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 12:** A²c0+Ac1+c2*exp(Ac3)+c4*log(c5*|A+c6|+1). Log term, no fractional powers. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 13:** A^(7/3)*c0/(Ac1+c2) + A^(4/3)*c3/(Ac1+c2) + A²c4/(Ac1+c2) + Ac5/(Ac1+c2) + Ac6/(Ac1+c2) + c7/(Ac1+c2) + c8/(Ac1+c2)

This is (A^(7/3)*c0 + A^(4/3)*c3 + A²*c4 + A*(c5+c6) + (c7+c8)) / (A*c1+c2)

Let me set c1=0, c2=1 (denominator=1): then we get A^(7/3)*c0 + A^(4/3)*c3 + A²*c4 + A*(c5+c6) + (c7+c8). Has A^(4/3) and A^(7/3) but not A^(1/3) or A^(1/2). 

What if c1≠0? Then dividing by (Ac1+c2) changes powers. For example A^(7/3)/(Ac1+c2) is not a simple power. Can partial fractions help? No, because we have fractional powers. This won't produce A^(1/3) and A^(1/2) simultaneously. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 14:** A²c0+Ac1+Ac2/(Ac3+c4)+c5*exp(Ac6). No fractional powers. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 15:** A²c0+Ac1+A^c2*c3/(A^c2+c4)+c5*exp(Ac6)
Set c6=0 → c5*1=c5 (constant). A^c2*c3/(A^c2+c4) - this is a sigmoid-like function of A^c2. 
We need A^(1/3)+A^(1/2)+A². The A² term is there. Can A^c2/(A^c2+c4) produce both A^(1/3) and A^(1/2)? No, it's a single term. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 16:** A²c0+Ac1+c2*exp(Ac3)+c4*log(Ac5+1). No fractional powers. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 17:** A^(1/3)*c0 + A²*c1 + A*c2 + c3*exp(A*c4) + c5
Set c2=0, c3=0 (or c4→-∞ but that's not clean, set c3=0). Left with A^(1/3)*c0 + A²*c1 + c5. Has A^(1/3) and A², but missing A^(1/2). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 18-19:** Complex rational/log expressions. Let me check if they can produce fractional powers... No, they involve integer powers and log/exp. **NO MATCH** for both.

**Candidate 20:** c0 + c1*sqrt(|A|) + c2*exp(c3*sin(Ac4+c5))
With A≥0: c0 + c1*sqrt(A) + c2*exp(c3*sin(Ac4+c5)). The exp(sin) is bounded and oscillatory, can't match A^(1/3) or A^2 for all A. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 21:** Rational function of integer powers of A. Can't produce A^(1/3) or A^(1/2). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 24:** With A≥0, |A|=A. Terms involve A^(4/3), A^(4/3)*A=A^(7/3), A, A², A^(1/2)=sqrt(A)... wait, let me look more carefully.

A^(4/3)*c0/(c1*A+1) + A^(4/3)*c2*A/(c1*A+1) + A*c3/(c1*A+1) + A*c4*A/(c1*A+1) + c5*A/(c1*A+1) + c6/(c1*A+1) + c7/(c1*A+1)

= (A^(4/3)*c0 + A^(7/3)*c2 + A*c3 + A²*c4 + A*c5 + c6 + c7) / (c1*A+1)

This has A^(4/3) and A^(7/3) type terms, divided by linear. Still no A^(1/3) or A^(1/2). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 35:** A²c0+Ac1+A^c2*c3+c4*exp(Ac5)+c6

We need: 0.634*A^(1/3) - 0.201*A^(1/2) - 0.201*A²

We have A², A, A^c2, and constant. Set c1=0 (remove A), c6=0 (remove constant). Left with A²*c0 + A^c2*c3. This gives us two terms: A² and A^c2. But we need THREE distinct power terms (A^(1/3), A^(1/2), A²). We only have two free power-law terms. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 46:** Ac0+Ac1*|A|^c2+c3*sin(Ac4+c5)+c6*|A|^c2
With A≥0: Ac0+c1*A^(1+c2)+c3*sin(Ac4+c5)+c6*A^c2

We need A^(1/3), A^(1/2), A². 
Set c3=0 (remove sin). Left with: A*c0 + c1*A^(1+c2) + c6*A^c2.

Three power terms: A^1, A^(1+c2), A^c2. 
Set c2=1/3: terms are A, A^(4/3), A^(1/3). Not matching (need A^(1/2) and A²).
Set c2=1: terms are A, A², A. Not enough distinct terms.
Set c2=1/2: terms are A, A^(3/2), A^(1/2). Missing A^(1/3) and A².

We need three specific powers: 1/3, 1/2, 2. We have three terms with powers: 1, c2, 1+c2. For any single c2, we get {1, c2, 1+c2}. We need {1/3, 1/2, 2}. 
- If c2=1/3: {1, 1/3, 4/3} ≠ {1/3, 1/2, 2}
- If c2=1/2: {1, 1/2, 3/2} ≠ {1/3, 1/2, 2}
- If c2=2: {1, 2, 3} ≠ {1/3, 1/2, 2}
- If c2=-1/2: {1, -1/2, 1/2} no
- If c2=1: {1, 1, 2} only two distinct

We can't get {1/3, 1/2, 2} from {1, c2, 1+c2} for any c2. But wait, we could set c0=0 to remove the A term. Then we have {c2, 1+c2}. That's only two terms, but we need three. **NO MATCH**

For general c2, this is complex. Let me try polynomial long division or specific values.

But dividing by (A+c2) doesn't create new irrational powers cleanly. The result would involve A^c0/(A+c2) type terms which aren't simple power functions. **NO MATCH**
